###begin article-title 0
###xml 20 24 20 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 99 115 99 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 99 115 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
Recombineering with tolC as a Selectable/Counter-selectable Marker: remodeling the rRNA Operons of Escherichia coli
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 0 16 0 16 <!--CREATIVE COMMONS-->
CREATIVE COMMONSThis is an Open Access article distributed under the terms of the Creative Commons Attribution Non-Commercial License () which permits unrestricted non-commercial use, distribution, and reproduction in any medium, provided the original work is properly cited.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 122 138 122 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 333 339 333 334 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</bold>
###xml 339 345 334 340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 391 395 386 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 433 440 428 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 776 783 771 778 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 864 867 859 862 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 938 942 933 937 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrlC</italic>
###xml 1191 1195 1186 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 122 138 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 433 440 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 776 783 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
This work describes the novel use of tolC as a selectable/counter-selectable marker for the facile modification of DNA in Escherichia coli. Expression of TolC (an outer membrane protein) confers relative resistance to toxic small molecules, while its absence renders the cell tolerant to colicin E1. These features, coupled with the lambdaredgam recombination system, allow for selection of tolC insertions/deletions anywhere on the E. coli chromosome or on plasmid DNA. This methodology obviates the need for minimal growth media, specialized wash protocols and the lengthy incubation times required by other published recombineering methods. As a rigorous test of the TolC selection system, six out of seven 23S rRNA genes were consecutively and seamlessly removed from the E. coli chromosome without affecting expression of neighboring genes within the complex rrn operons. The resulting plasmid-free strain retains one 23S rRNA gene (rrlC) in its natural location on the chromosome and is the first mutant of its kind. These new rRNA mutants will be useful in the study of rRNA gene regulation and ribosome function. Given its high efficiency, low background and facility in rich media, tolC selection is a broadly applicable method for the modification of DNA by recombineering.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
INTRODUCTION
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 54 70 54 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 156 157 156 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 158 159 158 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 262 263 262 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 289 293 289 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 324 327 324 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mar</italic>
###xml 328 331 328 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 341 342 341 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 412 416 412 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 418 419 418 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 420 421 420 421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 553 554 553 554 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 555 556 555 556 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 695 696 695 696 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 803 805 803 805 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 880 882 880 882 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 1007 1009 1007 1009 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 1010 1012 1010 1012 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 1031 1033 1031 1033 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1034 1036 1034 1036 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 1061 1063 1061 1063 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 1064 1066 1064 1066 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 1072 1079 1072 1079 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 54 70 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 1072 1079 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The tolC gene resides in an operon at 68.5 min on the Escherichia coli chromosome and precedes three non-essential open reading frames of unknown function (1,2). Sequence analysis and expression profiling postulate tolC to be transcribed from a tandem promoter (3). One study reports that tolC may fall under control of the mar-sox regulon (4), and other studies suggest the two-component system EvgAB regulates tolC (5,6). The gene itself encodes a 493 amino acid outer membrane protein with a signal sequence that allows SecB-dependent translocation (7,8). Once in the periplasm, mature TolC monomers undergo factor-independent assembly to form trimers subsequent to outer membrane insertion (9). Electron microscopy and X-ray crystallography have revealed a unique structure and topography for TolC (10) with the trimer existing as a trans-periplasmic tunnel, 140 A in length (11). Upon interaction with various inner-membrane pumps and translocases, TolC plays an important role in hemolysin secretion (12,13), protein import (14,15) and antibiotic efflux (10,16). In E. coli for instance, the AcrB-TolC efflux system pumps a diverse set of small molecules from the cell that include novobiocin, erythromycin and sodium dodecyl sulfate (SDS).
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 164 166 164 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 223 225 223 225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 393 395 393 395 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 544 546 544 546 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 660 667 660 667 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 747 749 747 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 750 752 750 752 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 943 945 943 945 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 660 667 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In addition to its role in expelling toxic compounds from the cell, surface-exposed loops of the TolC channel provide for specific interactions with bacteriophage (17) and for the import of bacteriocins such as colicin E1 (18). Bacteriocins are bactericidal proteins that constitute part of an antimicrobial defense system and can be found in most bacterial genera and in the archaea as well (19). Most bacteriocins are large proteins and, in the case of colicins, the genes encoding these toxins reside typically on extrachromosomal elements (20). Group A colicins demonstrate diverse mechanisms of action and have a narrow killing spectrum. They bind to the E. coli vitamin B receptor BtuB and are dependent upon the Tol proteins for transport (15,21). Colicin E1 (522 amino acids in length) requires TolC exclusively for access to the cytoplasmic membrane where it forms voltage-gated ion channels to disrupt the bilayer and kill the cell (22).
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 10 13 10 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tol</italic>
###xml 45 48 45 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tol</italic>
###xml 65 67 65 67 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 267 270 267 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tol</italic>
###xml 409 411 409 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 477 482 477 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC'</italic>
The first tol mutants demonstrated a colicin tolerant phenotype (18). Such mutants lost their sensitivity to particular colicins but fully maintained the ability to adsorb toxin on the cell surface through BtuB. Mutations at the tolC locus differ from those at other tol loci, in that they make the cell tolerant only to colicin E1, while such mutants respond with full sensitivity to other group A colicins (23). It is precisely these features that form the basis for testing tolC's utility as a selectable/counter-selectable marker in genome engineering studies.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 88 95 88 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 117 122 117 122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24 B25 B26 B27 B28">24&#8211;28</xref>
###xml 212 214 207 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 297 304 292 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 403 405 398 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 660 665 655 660 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31 B32 B33 B34 B35 B36">31&#8211;36</xref>
###xml 759 763 754 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">galK</italic>
###xml 768 772 763 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thyA</italic>
###xml 894 896 889 891 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 897 899 892 894 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 174 194 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">bacteriophage lambda</span>
###xml 297 304 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Recent years have witnessed remarkable advances in the application of new tools for the in vivo manipulation of DNA (24-28). Perhaps the most efficient of these tools is the bacteriophage lambda-Red recombinase (29). This system has been used to 'recombineer' genomic and extra chromosomal DNA in E. coli through simple introduction of double- or single-stranded DNA substrates into the bacterial cell (30). The efficiency of the system is enhanced greatly by the incorporation of selectable genetic markers to assist in the identification of desired recombinants and a number of methods exist for constructing point mutations, deletions and in-frame fusions (31-36). Recent work has demonstrated continued improvements to these approaches such as the use of galK and thyA. These genes encode single open reading frames each able to function as both a selectable and counter-selectable marker (37,38), but some practical limitations remain. Current protocols for these markers involve extensive washing of cells and the use of specialized media during selection. In addition, the requirement of minimal media for cell growth often results in a delay of 2-3 days before new mutant colonies can be chosen for further manipulation.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 48 52 48 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 145 152 145 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 365 369 365 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 489 496 489 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 606 613 606 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 145 152 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 489 496 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 606 613 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The following report describes the novel use of tolC as a selectable/counter-selectable marker for recombination-mediated genetic engineering in E. coli. This new system maintains the flexibility and efficiency of the latest recombineering approaches while eliminating the need for specialized media and extended incubation times. To demonstrate the utility of the tolC single-gene marker system, deletions, point mutations and gene fusions were made to a variety of coding regions on the E. coli chromosome and on plasmid DNA. In addition, six of the seven 23S rRNA genes were seamlessly deleted from the E. coli genome using one universal recombination cassette. The resulting strain (containing a single functioning 23S rRNA gene) shows no polar effects on rRNA transcription and serves as a new tool for the study of rRNA gene regulation and ribosome function.
###end p 8
###begin title 9
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 9
###begin title 10
Bacterial strains
###end title 10
###begin p 11
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 30 48 30 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;lacU169, nadA</italic>
###xml 52 62 48 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10, gal490</italic>
###xml 71 72 62 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 73 76 64 67 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">857</sub>
###xml 83 90 70 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cro-bio</italic>
###xml 127 129 114 116 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 271 279 253 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gam, bet</italic>
###xml 284 287 266 269 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exo</italic>
###xml 321 322 303 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 323 326 305 308 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">857</sub>
###xml 432 433 414 415 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 429 433 411 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nad<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 520 522 502 504 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 0 16 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
Escherichia coli DY329 (W3110 DeltalacU169, nadA::Tn10, gal490, lambda cI857 Delta[cro-bio]) was a generous gift of Don Court (28) and used with permission under US Public Health Service License Number L-159-2006/0. It contains a defective lambda prophage expressing the gam, bet and exo recombination functions from the cI857 regulated pL promoter. All bacterial strains constructed during this work are derivatives of RS205 (a nad+ derivative of strain DY329) that was engineered according to the methods outlined in (39). A list of all bacterial strains can be found in Supplementary Data, Table S1.
###end p 11
###begin title 12
Media and reagents
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 123 125 123 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 760 762 759 761 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
Bacterial strains were propagated on Luria Bertani broth and agar (Difco, BD Biosciences Franklin Lakes, NJ) according to (40). Agar plates for SDS (Fluka, Switzerland) selection were prepared according to standard procedures with an optimal concentration of 0.01% (w/v). Colicin E1 (SigmaAldrich St Louis, MO) selection was performed in 0.1 ml broth at a final concentration of 2 units/mul (see subsequently). DNA oligonucleotides were purchased from Integrated DNA Technologies (Coralville, IA) and a list describing their attributes can be found in Supplementary Data, Table S2. Linear dsDNA substrates were prepared using the GC-Rich PCR system (Roche Applied Science Indianapolis, IA) and purified following electrophoresis according to standard methods (41) using the WizardSV-Gel Clean-Up system (Promega Madison, WI). All PCR screening was performed with JumpStart REDTaq Ready Mix (SigmaAldrich) on purified, single bacterial colonies. Antibiotics and other bulk chemicals were purchased from SigmaAldrich.
###end p 13
###begin title 14
Linear DNA substrate design, redgam induction and selection of recombinants
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 63 70 63 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 114 120 114 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 297 305 297 305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 552 556 552 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 556 557 556 557 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 690 692 690 692 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 696 705 696 705 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 1.</label>
###xml 717 721 717 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 731 738 731 738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>

###xml 2251 2255 2232 2236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 2296 2300 2277 2281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">recA</italic>
###xml 2338 2342 2319 2323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">recA</italic>
###xml 2425 2428 2406 2409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ara</italic>
###xml 2438 2442 2419 2423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dicB</italic>
###xml 2447 2451 2428 2432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ygeX</italic>
###xml 2494 2498 2475 2479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 2572 2576 2553 2557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 2614 2622 2595 2603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2649 2653 2630 2634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 705 2829 705 2810 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="16">Deletion of <italic>tolC</italic> from the <italic>E. coli</italic> genome and cassette design. Fragments of chromosomal DNA are depicted with bent lines. Target genes (<italic>tolC</italic> and <italic>recA</italic>) are denoted by colored boxes; neighboring genes that encode open reading frames are shown with shaded boxes. P2 and P1 refer to the promoters of <italic>tolC</italic>; P<italic><sub>nudF</sub></italic> and P<italic><sub>recA</sub></italic> drive expression of the <italic>nudF</italic> and <italic>recA</italic> genes, respectively. (<bold>A</bold>) Strategy for deleting <italic>tolC</italic> from the chromosome. Recombination using the single-stranded DNA molecule &#916;<italic>tolC</italic> Oligo (Rx-P15) and &#955; <italic>redgam</italic> is depicted. The Rx-P15 oligo contains 35 bases of DNA directly homologous to sequences flanking <italic>tolC</italic> on the chromosome (curvy lines). The dotted line in Rx-P15 is merely a representation demonstrating that the two halves of the 70-base oligo are contiguous. Large X's denote &#955; <italic>red</italic>-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. Following recombination and selection for colicin E1 resistance, the deletion of <italic>tolC</italic> from the genome was confirmed by PCR with primers shown as brown arrows (Rx-P19 and -P20). (<bold>B</bold>) Amplification of the <italic>tolC</italic> cassette and deletion of <italic>recA</italic>. Oligo 1 (RxP-43) and Oligo 2 (Rx-P44) PCR amplify a double-stranded <italic>tolC</italic> expression cassette. ORF X-change oligo (Rx-P45) is used with RX-P46 (data not shown) to amplify only the <italic>tolC</italic> open reading frame without its promoter. Curvy lines represent homologous DNA shared by the linear DNA substrate and the bacterial chromosome while large X's again denote &#955; <italic>red</italic>-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. In this example, the <italic>tolC</italic> expression cassette replaces the entire <italic>recA</italic> transcription unit (red) or only the <italic>recA</italic> ORF (purple) conferring SDS resistance. A similar strategy was used to delete the <italic>ara</italic> regulon, <italic>dicB</italic> and <italic>ygeX</italic> (data not shown). PCR primers internal to <italic>tolC</italic> and complementary to neighboring genes were used to confirm insertion of <italic>tolC</italic> and deletion of the target gene (see <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref> for an example). Removing <italic>tolC</italic> from its new location followed the methodology in (A) above. The sequence and description of all primers and oligos can be found in Table S2. Illustrations not drawn to scale.</p>

###xml 2866 2882 2847 2863 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 2899 2903 2880 2884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 3143 3147 3124 3128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrlC</italic>
###xml 3185 3189 3166 3170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 3267 3271 3248 3252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 3452 3460 3433 3441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 3489 3493 3470 3474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 3950 3954 3931 3935 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</sub>
###xml 3950 3954 3931 3935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>tolC</sub></italic>
###xml 4044 4054 4025 4035 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gltU, aspT</italic>
###xml 4059 4063 4040 4044 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trpT</italic>
###xml 4077 4081 4058 4062 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrsC</italic>
###xml 4086 4090 4067 4071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrfC</italic>
###xml 4450 4453 4426 4429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">red</italic>
###xml 2838 4542 2819 4518 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="17">Strategy for remodeling the <italic>Escherichia coli</italic> rRNA operons. A <italic>tolC</italic> cassette is shown amplified by rrlX oligos For and Rev (Rx-P50 and -P51, respectively) having universal homology arms that correspond to sequences flanking the 23S rRNA genes from all seven operons (Figure S3). In this example, removal of <italic>rrlC</italic> occurs following introduction of the <italic>tolC</italic> cassette and recombination. SDS-resistant colonies are screened by PCR using <italic>tolC</italic> Chk primer1 (Rx-P71) paired with an operon-specific primer (Px-P52 through P58). This screening can be multiplexed as primers were designed to amplify fragments of distinct sizes (<xref ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>). Following confirmation of <italic>tolC</italic> insertion, the cassette is removed by introducing universal single-stranded oligos (RX-P59 or P60, depending on the direction of replication). After selecting for colicin E1 resistance, transformants are screened by plating on SDS and by PCR using a 16S rDNA primer with the operon specific primers mentioned before. Fragments of chromosomal DNA are depicted with bent lines. P2 and P1 refer to the promoters that drive expression of the rRNA operons and P<italic><sub>tolC</sub></italic> represents the P1 promoter for that gene. Neighboring genes are shown with shaded boxes: <italic>gltU, aspT</italic> and <italic>trpT</italic> encode tRNA; <italic>rrsC</italic> and <italic>rrfC</italic> encodes 16S and 5S rRNA, respectively. Green diamonds represent RNase III processing sites. Blue diamonds represent RNAse E processing sites for tRNA and 5S RNA. Primers used for PCR screening are shown with brown arrows. Curvy lines represent homologous DNA shared by the linear DNA substrate and the bacterial chromosome while large X's again denote &#955; <italic>red</italic>-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. Illustrations not drawn to scale.</p>

###xml 4542 4551 4518 4527 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 3.</label>
###xml 4588 4589 4564 4565 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 4654 4661 4630 4637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 4688 4691 4664 4667 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
###xml 4824 4832 4788 4796 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 5064 5068 5020 5024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnC</italic>
###xml 5152 5153 5108 5109 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 5315 5319 5271 5275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnC</italic>
###xml 5329 5333 5285 5289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnG</italic>
###xml 5343 5347 5299 5303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnE</italic>

###xml 63 70 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 731 738 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2866 2882 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 4654 4661 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The tolC gene was removed from its location at 68.5 min on the E. coli chromosome by linear DNA transformation of redgam-induced cells with a 70-base single-stranded oligonucleotide (Rx-P15) of the following sequence: 5'-TTTCAGCGACGTTTGACTGCCGTTTGAGCAGTC-ATATGACGACGACGGGGCTTCGGCCCCGTCTGAACGT-3' (Figure 1A). Colicin E1 selection was performed (see subsequently) and transformants were screened by PCR for the presence of a 310 base-pair (bp) product using Primers Rx-P19 (5'-GTTTCTCGTGCAATAATTTCTACATC-3') and Rx-P20 (5'-CGTATGGATTTTGTCCGTTTCA-3'). A tolC- phenotype was confirmed by patching single colonies on 0.01% SDS agar and by cross streak against colicin E1 [plate receptor test- (23)]. Figure 1.Deletion of tolC from the E. coli genome and cassette design. Fragments of chromosomal DNA are depicted with bent lines. Target genes (tolC and recA) are denoted by colored boxes; neighboring genes that encode open reading frames are shown with shaded boxes. P2 and P1 refer to the promoters of tolC; PnudF and PrecA drive expression of the nudF and recA genes, respectively. (A) Strategy for deleting tolC from the chromosome. Recombination using the single-stranded DNA molecule DeltatolC Oligo (Rx-P15) and lambda redgam is depicted. The Rx-P15 oligo contains 35 bases of DNA directly homologous to sequences flanking tolC on the chromosome (curvy lines). The dotted line in Rx-P15 is merely a representation demonstrating that the two halves of the 70-base oligo are contiguous. Large X's denote lambda red-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. Following recombination and selection for colicin E1 resistance, the deletion of tolC from the genome was confirmed by PCR with primers shown as brown arrows (Rx-P19 and -P20). (B) Amplification of the tolC cassette and deletion of recA. Oligo 1 (RxP-43) and Oligo 2 (Rx-P44) PCR amplify a double-stranded tolC expression cassette. ORF X-change oligo (Rx-P45) is used with RX-P46 (data not shown) to amplify only the tolC open reading frame without its promoter. Curvy lines represent homologous DNA shared by the linear DNA substrate and the bacterial chromosome while large X's again denote lambda red-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. In this example, the tolC expression cassette replaces the entire recA transcription unit (red) or only the recA ORF (purple) conferring SDS resistance. A similar strategy was used to delete the ara regulon, dicB and ygeX (data not shown). PCR primers internal to tolC and complementary to neighboring genes were used to confirm insertion of tolC and deletion of the target gene (see Figure 2 for an example). Removing tolC from its new location followed the methodology in (A) above. The sequence and description of all primers and oligos can be found in Table S2. Illustrations not drawn to scale.Figure 2.Strategy for remodeling the Escherichia coli rRNA operons. A tolC cassette is shown amplified by rrlX oligos For and Rev (Rx-P50 and -P51, respectively) having universal homology arms that correspond to sequences flanking the 23S rRNA genes from all seven operons (Figure S3). In this example, removal of rrlC occurs following introduction of the tolC cassette and recombination. SDS-resistant colonies are screened by PCR using tolC Chk primer1 (Rx-P71) paired with an operon-specific primer (Px-P52 through P58). This screening can be multiplexed as primers were designed to amplify fragments of distinct sizes (Figure 3). Following confirmation of tolC insertion, the cassette is removed by introducing universal single-stranded oligos (RX-P59 or P60, depending on the direction of replication). After selecting for colicin E1 resistance, transformants are screened by plating on SDS and by PCR using a 16S rDNA primer with the operon specific primers mentioned before. Fragments of chromosomal DNA are depicted with bent lines. P2 and P1 refer to the promoters that drive expression of the rRNA operons and PtolC represents the P1 promoter for that gene. Neighboring genes are shown with shaded boxes: gltU, aspT and trpT encode tRNA; rrsC and rrfC encodes 16S and 5S rRNA, respectively. Green diamonds represent RNase III processing sites. Blue diamonds represent RNAse E processing sites for tRNA and 5S RNA. Primers used for PCR screening are shown with brown arrows. Curvy lines represent homologous DNA shared by the linear DNA substrate and the bacterial chromosome while large X's again denote lambda red-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. Illustrations not drawn to scale.Figure 3.Confirmation of 23S rRNA deletions. (A) Agarose gel showing PCR products generated from gDNA of select E. coli strains. Strain RS526 (WT rrl) has all rRNA operons intact and yields large (approximately4-5 kb) PCR products when the 16S and operon-specific primers are used (Figure 2). The DeltarrlDGH strain (RS547) shows smaller PCR fragments demonstrating the deletion of 23S rRNA genes from the respective operons. Lastly, strain RS676 (DeltarrlABDEGH) has only one copy of the gene for 23S rRNA located in the rrnC operon. Lanes 1 and 23: Marker DNA (1 kb ladder and 0.1 kb ladder, respectively). (B) Southern blot demonstrating the step-wise removal of 23S rRNA genes from six of the seven operons. The sizes of the DNA bands and corresponding operons follow: rrnC-16.9 kb; rrnG-15.5 kb; rrnE-11.2 kb; rrnH-9.6 kb; rrnD-8.1 kb; rrnB-7.2 kb and rrnA-6.6 kb. Strain designations: WT- RS526, Delta1- RS537, Delta2- RS544, Delta3- RS547, Delta4- RS550, Delta5- RS554 and Delta6-RS676.
###end p 15

Deletion of tolC from the E. coli genome and cassette design. Fragments of chromosomal DNA are depicted with bent lines. Target genes (tolC and recA) are denoted by colored boxes; neighboring genes that encode open reading frames are shown with shaded boxes. P2 and P1 refer to the promoters of tolC; PnudF and PrecA drive expression of the nudF and recA genes, respectively. (A) Strategy for deleting tolC from the chromosome. Recombination using the single-stranded DNA molecule DeltatolC Oligo (Rx-P15) and lambda redgam is depicted. The Rx-P15 oligo contains 35 bases of DNA directly homologous to sequences flanking tolC on the chromosome (curvy lines). The dotted line in Rx-P15 is merely a representation demonstrating that the two halves of the 70-base oligo are contiguous. Large X's denote lambda red-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. Following recombination and selection for colicin E1 resistance, the deletion of tolC from the genome was confirmed by PCR with primers shown as brown arrows (Rx-P19 and -P20). (B) Amplification of the tolC cassette and deletion of recA. Oligo 1 (RxP-43) and Oligo 2 (Rx-P44) PCR amplify a double-stranded tolC expression cassette. ORF X-change oligo (Rx-P45) is used with RX-P46 (data not shown) to amplify only the tolC open reading frame without its promoter. Curvy lines represent homologous DNA shared by the linear DNA substrate and the bacterial chromosome while large X's again denote lambda red-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. In this example, the tolC expression cassette replaces the entire recA transcription unit (red) or only the recA ORF (purple) conferring SDS resistance. A similar strategy was used to delete the ara regulon, dicB and ygeX (data not shown). PCR primers internal to tolC and complementary to neighboring genes were used to confirm insertion of tolC and deletion of the target gene (see Figure 2 for an example). Removing tolC from its new location followed the methodology in (A) above. The sequence and description of all primers and oligos can be found in Table S2. Illustrations not drawn to scale.

###xml 28 44 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
Strategy for remodeling the Escherichia coli rRNA operons. A tolC cassette is shown amplified by rrlX oligos For and Rev (Rx-P50 and -P51, respectively) having universal homology arms that correspond to sequences flanking the 23S rRNA genes from all seven operons (Figure S3). In this example, removal of rrlC occurs following introduction of the tolC cassette and recombination. SDS-resistant colonies are screened by PCR using tolC Chk primer1 (Rx-P71) paired with an operon-specific primer (Px-P52 through P58). This screening can be multiplexed as primers were designed to amplify fragments of distinct sizes (Figure 3). Following confirmation of tolC insertion, the cassette is removed by introducing universal single-stranded oligos (RX-P59 or P60, depending on the direction of replication). After selecting for colicin E1 resistance, transformants are screened by plating on SDS and by PCR using a 16S rDNA primer with the operon specific primers mentioned before. Fragments of chromosomal DNA are depicted with bent lines. P2 and P1 refer to the promoters that drive expression of the rRNA operons and PtolC represents the P1 promoter for that gene. Neighboring genes are shown with shaded boxes: gltU, aspT and trpT encode tRNA; rrsC and rrfC encodes 16S and 5S rRNA, respectively. Green diamonds represent RNase III processing sites. Blue diamonds represent RNAse E processing sites for tRNA and 5S RNA. Primers used for PCR screening are shown with brown arrows. Curvy lines represent homologous DNA shared by the linear DNA substrate and the bacterial chromosome while large X's again denote lambda red-mediated cross-over between regions of homologous DNA. Illustrations not drawn to scale.
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 37 38 37 38 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 103 110 103 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 137 140 137 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
###xml 273 281 261 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 513 517 493 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnC</italic>
###xml 601 602 581 582 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 764 768 744 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnC</italic>
###xml 778 782 758 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnG</italic>
###xml 792 796 772 776 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnE</italic>
###xml 806 810 786 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnH</italic>
###xml 819 823 799 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnD</italic>
###xml 832 836 812 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnB</italic>
###xml 848 852 828 832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnA</italic>
###xml 103 110 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Confirmation of 23S rRNA deletions. (A) Agarose gel showing PCR products generated from gDNA of select E. coli strains. Strain RS526 (WT rrl) has all rRNA operons intact and yields large (approximately4-5 kb) PCR products when the 16S and operon-specific primers are used (Figure 2). The DeltarrlDGH strain (RS547) shows smaller PCR fragments demonstrating the deletion of 23S rRNA genes from the respective operons. Lastly, strain RS676 (DeltarrlABDEGH) has only one copy of the gene for 23S rRNA located in the rrnC operon. Lanes 1 and 23: Marker DNA (1 kb ladder and 0.1 kb ladder, respectively). (B) Southern blot demonstrating the step-wise removal of 23S rRNA genes from six of the seven operons. The sizes of the DNA bands and corresponding operons follow: rrnC-16.9 kb; rrnG-15.5 kb; rrnE-11.2 kb; rrnH-9.6 kb; rrnD-8.1 kb; rrnB-7.2 kb and rrnA-6.6 kb. Strain designations: WT- RS526, Delta1- RS537, Delta2- RS544, Delta3- RS547, Delta4- RS550, Delta5- RS554 and Delta6-RS676.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 26 30 26 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 217 219 217 219 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 254 256 254 256 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 455 463 455 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 532 536 532 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 653 657 653 657 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 775 777 775 777 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 813 815 813 815 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 848 849 848 849 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</sup>
###xml 908 912 908 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1070 1074 1070 1074 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
A cassette containing the tolC gene (and upstream promoter sequence) was amplified by PCR from strain RS205 gDNA to serve directly as a linear DNA substrate. Primer design adhered to the following general scheme: 5'-N50-TTGAGGCACATTAACGCCCTAT-3' and 5'-N50-CCCCGTCGTCGTCATCAG-3', where 'N' represents nucleotides comprising the homology arms necessary for recombination. These tails share sequence identity with the regions of DNA flanking a target gene (Figure 1B). A 1.62 kb PCR product is generated using such primers and allows tolC expression when integrated into the chromosome (or plasmid DNA) via the 50-bp long tails. For experiments where the tolC ORF is used for exchange with a target open reading frame (i.e. no promoter), the following primer pair is used: 5'-N50-ATGAAGAAATTGCTCCCCATTCT-3' and 5'-N50-TCAGTTACGGAAAGGGTTATGACC-3'. SDSR transformants are then screened for proper positioning of tolC using PCR with primers specific for regions flanking the target gene. Appropriate chromosomal rearrangements are confirmed by DNA sequencing. Removal of the tolC cassette followed the general strategy outlined in the previous paragraph.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
General recombineering with tolC as a selectable and counter-selectable marker
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 87 89 87 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 90 92 90 92 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 220 223 214 217 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 333 339 316 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
RS205 and other derivatives were prepared for recombineering essentially as described (28,39). Briefly, cells were diluted 1/50 from a fresh overnight culture in LB broth at 35degreesC and grown to between 0.3 and 0.4 OD600. The pL promoter was de-repressed by incubation at 42degreesC for 15 min with optimal induction of the lambdaredgam genes requiring longer incubation for some of the 23S rRNA mutants (see Results section for further detail). Induced cultures were chilled by constant swirling in an ice/water bath for 5-10 min and cells were pelleted by centrifugation. Cell pellets were washed in 2x their original volume of ice-cold water, pelleted and washed again in 1/20 their original volume with ice-cold water. After a final centrifugation step in a 1.5 ml microfuge tube, cells were resuspended to 1/100 their original volume in ice-cold water and used immediately for electroporation.
###end p 21
###begin p 22
For linear DNA transformation, 50 mul of cell suspension was mixed with approximately100 ng DNA, transferred to a pre-chilled electroporation cuvette (1 mm), and pulsed at 1.8 kV in a Biorad Gene Pulser Xcell (Hercules, CA). Cells were transferred to a 15 ml tube (Falcon 2059) containing 1 ml LB and placed at 35degreesC with shaking for outgrowth.
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 13 17 13 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 17 18 17 18 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 176 177 174 175 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sup>
###xml 190 191 188 189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 230 231 228 229 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">8</sup>
###xml 261 262 259 260 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</sup>
Selection of tolC+ recombinants was performed after a 2-h incubation followed by plating </= 0.1 ml onto LB agar containing 0.01% SDS. Most experiments yielded between 1.6 x 104 and 2.3 x 106 SDS-resistant transformants per 5 x 108 total cells. Selection of SDSR transformants for some of the 23S rRNA mutants required extended outgrowth times (see text).
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 26 30 26 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
To select for loss of the tolC marker, cells were incubated after electroporation for 5 h to allow for TolC turnover. Typically, 10 mul of cells was then transferred to a fresh tube containing 65 mul of LB and 200 units colicin E1 and incubated for 60 min at 35degreesC with shaking. Aliquots are plated on LB agar and grown overnight at 35degreesC. Most experiments yielded colicin-resistant recombinants at an approximately0.015 frequency. The colicin E1 tolerance of the resulting recombinants can be confirmed by a modified plate receptor test where, for instance, a 15 mul line of colicin E1 (8 units/mul) is pipetted down the center of an LB plate and each transformant is cross-streaked using a flat toothpick. Sensitivity was scored as a clear zone over the colicin E1 line.
###end p 24
###begin title 25
Preliminary characterization of engineered rRNA mutants
###end title 25
###begin p 26
###xml 44 46 44 46 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 212 215 212 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bam</italic>
###xml 222 225 222 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pst</italic>
###xml 228 230 228 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 428 430 428 430 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
Southern blots were performed as described (41) using standard procedures. Genomic DNA samples were prepared using the DNeasy Blood and Tissue kit (Qiagen Valencia, CA) and treated with restriction endonucleases BamHI and PstI (42). The 23S rDNA region from HpaI to SalI was PCR amplified from strain RS205 with the following primers 5'-ACGCTTCTCGCTCTCAACC-3' (Rx-P200) and 5'-GAATAGGGGAGCCGAAGGG-3' (Rx-P201) then labeled with 32P-NTP for use as probe.
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 279 280 273 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
###xml 280 283 274 277 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gen</sub>
###xml 288 289 282 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 321 322 315 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 329 330 323 324 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</sub>
###xml 328 330 322 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X<sub>t</sub></italic>
###xml 334 335 328 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X</italic>
###xml 335 336 329 330 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 349 350 343 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X</italic>
###xml 497 499 491 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
Growth characteristics of the different rRNA mutants were determined by luminescence using BacTiter Glo (Promega) from 50 ml broth cultures in 250 ml Erlenmeyer flasks at 37degreesC using an orbital shaker set at 180 rpm. Doubling time was calculated according to the following: tgen = 1/k where the growth rate constant k = logXt-logX0/0.301t with X equal to cell number (lumens). Sensitivity to various antibiotics was assessed in LB broth according to CLSI procedures with minor modifications (43).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 68 70 68 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 118 121 118 121 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 213 214 205 206 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 497 498 489 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 611 612 597 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 612 615 598 601 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ave</sub>
###xml 752 753 732 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 753 756 733 736 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ave</sub>
###xml 944 950 918 924 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">260 nm</sub>
###xml 1056 1057 1030 1031 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
Ribosome isolation was performed according to published procedures (44). Briefly, cells were grown to mid/late log (OD600 </= 0.9) in LB medium at 37degreesC, concentrated by centrifugation, and frozen in liquid N2. One-gram cell pellets were resuspended in 10 ml of ice cold 1X TMK (10 mM Tris-Cl pH 7.5, 16 mM MgAc, 60 mM KAc, 1 mM DTT) and lysed at 20-25 000 psi using an EmulsiFlex C5 high pressure homogenizer (Avestin Inc. Ottawa, Canada). Cell lysate was cleared by centrifugation at 30 000g for 30 min at 4degreesC. Supernatant was mixed with sucrose to 220 mM final and centrifuged for 53 min at 90 000gave (4degreesC) to remove additional debris. Ribosomes were pelleted through a 20% v/v cushion of 1.1 M sucrose by centrifugation at 150 000gave for 18 h at 4degreesC, washed and resuspended in 1X TMK. A total of 10-30% sucrose gradients were prepared in 1X TMK using a Gradient Master (Biocomp Inc. Edenton, NJ) and ribosomes (2 OD260 nm units/0.1 ml) were analyzed following centrifugation in a SW60Ti rotor (Beckman Fullerton, CA) at 237 000g, 2 h, 7degreesC using a continuous flow UV monitor (Amersham Biosciences Piscataway, NJ).
###end p 28
###begin title 29
RESULTS
###end title 29
###begin title 30
###xml 13 17 13 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
Deleting the tolC promoter and coding region
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 35 39 35 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 126 130 126 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 190 194 190 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>

###xml 546 550 546 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>

###xml 901 905 901 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>

###xml 1043 1051 1043 1051 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1219 1223 1219 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1229 1233 1229 1233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nudF</italic>
###xml 1276 1280 1276 1280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>

###xml 1809 1830 1809 1830 <tr xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>tolC</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">N/A</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">N/A</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">ss Oligo</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">25%</td></tr>

###xml 239 246 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
As a first step in testing whether tolC could be used as both a positive and negative selectable marker, a strain lacking the tolC coding sequence was constructed. The strategy for removing tolC from its normal location at 68.5 min on the E. coli chromosome is shown in Figure 1A. Lambda recombineering was used to delete the gene, simultaneously demonstrating proof of principle for the strategy outlined earlier. Single-stranded DNA oligonucleotides were designed to have 35 bases of exact sequence homology to regions up and downstream of the tolC coding sequence. Recombination directed by this 70-base oligo (Rx-P15) would remove the tolC coding sequence in addition to its proximal promoter (P1), leaving the P2 promoter completely intact and slightly truncating the nudF promoter. When transformed to redgam-induced RS205 and selected for tolerance to colicin E1, Rx-P15 was able to remove the tolC gene with 25% efficiency (Table 1). Deletion of tolC was confirmed by PCR using primers directed against sequences within nudF and ygiB (Figure 1A) and the colicin E1 tolerance of the transformants was confirmed using the modified plate receptor test (data not shown). Oligonucleotide Rx-P17 (which leaves both P1tolC and PnudF intact) was just as efficient at removing tolC. When using DNA oligonucleotides exactly complementary to Rx-P15 and Rx-P17 (i.e. homologous to the lead replicating gDNA strand), tolC gene deletions were not detected under the same experimental conditions (data not shown). Thus, selection for tolC removal is possible through the use of colicin E1 and the resulting strain, RS206, can be used to test tolC's efficiency as a positive selectable marker. Table 1.Recombineering with tolCTargetInsertion methodEfficiency of tolC insertionDeletion methodEfficiency of tolC removaltolCN/AN/Ass Oligo25%recAPtolC Cassette100%ss Oligo86%recAPtolC Cassette100%ds PCR product100%araCBADPtolC Cassette100%ss Oligo77%dicBPtolC Cassette100%ss Oligo89%ygeXPtolC Cassette100%ss OligoNDrrICPtolC Cassette13%ss Oligo100%recAtolC ORF-Xchange100%NDNDdicBtolC ORF-Xchange0%NDNDygeXtolC ORF-Xchange0%NDNDA list of target genes for testing the efficiency of the tolC selectable/counter-selectable marker system is shown in column one. The table lists the methods used to insert tolC (either through a promoter-containing tolC cassette or through ORF-X change) and the methods used to remove tolC (either by using a single-stranded oligo or a double-stranded PCR product). Confirmation of tolC insertion or removal was performed by PCR (see Figure S2 for primers), phenotype analysis, and DNA sequencing when appropriate. The efficiencies for each method were calculated as follows: (number of recombinants testing positive for the insertion or deletion event/total number of resistant colonies tested) x 100. Deletion of tolC following ORF-X change was not performed. ND: not determined.
###end p 31
