###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 80 83 80 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
###xml 207 214 207 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 588 591 588 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
###xml 671 674 671 674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
###xml 823 830 823 830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 846 849 846 849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
To determine whether the differences in ribosome profiles might confer upon the rrl mutant strains an easily testable phenotype, their sensitivity to a number of well-characterized antibiotics was measured (Table 2). The minimum inhibitory concentration (MIC) of the cell wall-targeting antibiotic ampicillin did not change for any of the mutants tested. Similarly, there is no difference in the MIC values for rifampin (targets RNA polymerase and transcription) and novobiocin (targets DNA gyrase and replication). These results suggest there is little, if any, detectable effect of the rrl mutants on essential cellular processes not relating to protein synthesis. The rrl mutants were also tested with drugs and antibiotics that block protein synthesis through binding to either the 30S or 50S subunits of the ribosome. Table 2 shows that all rrl mutants are comparable to WT in their sensitivity to ribosome targeting compounds under the conditions tested.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
DISCUSSION
###end title 51
###begin p 52
###xml 139 146 139 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 148 150 148 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 151 153 151 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 154 156 154 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 157 159 157 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 160 162 160 162 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 310 312 310 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 313 315 313 315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 316 318 316 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 319 321 319 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 441 445 441 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 139 146 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Genome engineering has undergone remarkable advances due to the development of efficient systems for recombination in model organisms like E. coli (25,27,28,48,49). It is now routine to create deletions and point mutations in target genes (on the chromosome or on plasmids) using DNA oligonucleotides and PCR (26,32,50,51). This study describes the development of novel methodology that uses the gene coding for a single open reading frame, tolC, as both a selectable and counter-selectable marker for genome engineering studies. TolC selection obviates the need for minimal media, specialized wash protocols, extended incubation times and the traditional antibiotic selections required by other techniques.
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 178 180 178 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B52">52</xref>
###xml 190 194 190 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 411 413 411 413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 572 578 567 573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 607 614 602 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 632 636 627 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 745 749 740 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 889 891 884 886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 963 967 958 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1083 1086 1078 1081 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;10</sup>
###xml 1093 1097 1088 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1132 1134 1127 1129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54">54</xref>
###xml 1158 1165 1153 1160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 1369 1376 1364 1371 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 1414 1418 1409 1413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1496 1500 1491 1495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1526 1532 1516 1522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 1562 1564 1552 1554 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 1565 1567 1555 1557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 1568 1570 1558 1560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 1843 1847 1833 1837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 2143 2145 2127 2129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 2146 2148 2130 2132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 2290 2297 2274 2281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 2314 2318 2298 2302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 607 614 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2290 2297 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Historically, selectable markers used in recombinant DNA work have been small genetic elements that express cytoplasmic enzymes or proteins conferring resistance to antibiotics (52). Use of tolC as a genetic marker is somewhat unorthodox in that the gene encodes an outer membrane protein that forms a transperiplasmic channel through which various efflux pumps extrude toxic molecules from the bacterial cell (10). TolC's properties, however, meet perfectly the requirements for use as a tool in genome engineering especially when coupled with the highly efficient lambdaredgam recombination system. In an E. coli cell deleted for tolC, SDS and other small toxic molecules are unable to be pumped efficiently from the cell. Introduction of the tolC ORF confers relative resistance to these compounds but for some molecules (e.g. novobiocin) spontaneous resistance mutants may also arise (53). Consequently, SDS was used in this work as the reagent to select for tolC insertions as it causes cell lysis and the frequency of spontaneous SDS-resistant mutants is extremely low (<5 x 10-10) in a tolC null background [data not shown, (54)]. Indeed, the data in Table 1 show that SDS selection results in 100% recombination efficiency at any unique targeted site and gives no background at SDS concentrations as low as 0.002% (data not shown). The efficiencies reported in Table 1 only reflect proper placement of the tolC cassette at the targeted site. The high frequency of recombination seen with tolC is governed by the lambdaredgam recombination system itself (28,32,55) and is not influenced by SDS selection. SDS selection is, however, economical and allows for facile incorporation into molten agar without the need for cooling to intermediate temperatures as is necessary with heat labile antibiotics. Furthermore, positive selection for tolC using SDS is performed on rich media (LB) commonly used in many laboratories. Therefore, recombinants often arise after only 16 h (overnight) incubation at 35degreesC. This incubation period is similar to other gene cassettes that select for chloramphenicol resistance or gentamycin resistance (30,36) but those markers are incapable of providing counter-selection. Finally, when creating mutants to study gene regulation or other aspects of E. coli physiology, the tolC strategy does not require antibiotics or specialized media that might interfere with facile experimental design or data interpretation (see subsequently).
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 61 68 61 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 249 251 249 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 255 257 255 257 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 258 260 258 260 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 261 263 261 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B52">52</xref>
###xml 264 266 264 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 267 269 267 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 416 424 416 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sacB-neo</italic>
###xml 493 495 493 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 578 582 578 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpsL</italic>
###xml 610 613 610 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo</italic>
###xml 657 659 657 659 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 704 708 704 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpsL</italic>
###xml 768 772 768 772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpsL</italic>
###xml 846 848 846 848 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 888 894 883 889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 929 933 924 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">galK</italic>
###xml 937 941 932 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thyA</italic>
###xml 955 962 950 957 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 964 966 959 961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 967 969 962 964 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 1242 1246 1237 1241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">galK</italic>
###xml 1251 1255 1246 1250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thyA</italic>
###xml 1537 1539 1532 1534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 1540 1542 1535 1537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 1543 1545 1538 1540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 61 68 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 955 962 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The key feature of TolC as a tool for genetic engineering in E. coli is the ability to select for its absence from the cell. A number of counter-selectable markers have been developed to perform genetic manipulation with varying degrees of success (31,32,34,35,52,56,57). Unlike tolC, these counter-selectable markers must be used in tandem with a gene that allows for positive selection. Though widely applied, the sacB-neo fusion cassette involves antibiotic selection and sucrose toxicity (24) which can result in high background after negative selection. Alternatively, the rpsL gene has been coupled with neo to provide concerted antibiotic selection (32). In a bacterial strain containing a mutant rpsL gene on the chromosome, loss of a second copy of wild-type rpsL converts the cell from streptomycin-sensitive to streptomycin-resistant (57). Two recent efforts coupled the lambdaredgam recombineering system with either galK or thyA selection in E. coli (37,38). These and other auxotrophic markers can be used quite readily in a positive selection mode, allowing recombinants having these markers integrated into the chromosome to grow on minimal media. Clever counter-selection methods were utilized to permit efficient removal of galK and thyA by incorporating 2-deoxygalactose and trimethoprim/thymine, respectively, into agar plates. Such methods, however, require extensive washing of cells to reduce background during positive selection (since minimal media is required) and recombinants appear only after 3-days growth (35,37,38).
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 9 13 9 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">galK</italic>
###xml 18 22 18 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thyA</italic>
###xml 39 43 39 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 274 276 274 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 307 311 307 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 370 374 370 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 478 480 478 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 481 483 481 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 484 486 484 486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
Like the galK and thyA techniques, the tolC system also provides for efficient counter-selection. Through its surfaced exposed residues, the TolC protein allows import of colicin E1, a bactericidal protein that normally functions as part of an antimicrobial defense system (14). Therefore, cells containing tolC are lysed when exposed to colicin E1. This feature of the tolC counter-selection strategy helps to reduce background without the need for specialized wash protocols (35,37,38). Furthermore, the procedure can be performed in rich media, allowing recombinants to grow after only 16 h incubation. The short incubation time is advantageous as it permits PCR screening of colonies and phenotypic testing for both SDS sensitivity and colicin E1 resistance/tolerance all within one workday following electroporation.
###end p 55
###begin p 56
###xml 59 63 59 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 202 209 202 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 242 246 242 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 294 301 294 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 403 407 403 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 731 735 731 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 871 875 871 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 951 957 951 957 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 959 961 959 961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 1105 1109 1105 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1119 1123 1119 1123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">recA</italic>
###xml 1186 1193 1186 1193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 1239 1243 1239 1243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 294 301 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The efficiency of colicin E1 counter-selection against the tolC cassette using single-stranded oligonucleotides is quite high, generally 80-100% for targets that map to various locations on the genome (Table 1 and data not shown). Removal of tolC from its normal location (using ss DNA) on the E. coli chromosome was, however, less efficient with only 25% of the E1-resistant recombinants demonstrating tolC deletion. The lower efficiency in this case could be due simply to sub-optimal recombineering conditions. Alternatively, genome position effects or the minimal length of the single stranded oligonucleotides used as a recombination substrate may have also contributed to the reduced efficiency. Increasing the efficiency of tolC deletion at this locus might be achieved by lengthening the ss-oligo to provide more than 35 bases of homologous sequence flanking the tolC target or by using double stranded DNA to increase homology further. Ellis et al. (55) showed that when using linear DNA in this way, recombination efficiency can improve with increased length, a fact confirmed by the removal of tolC from the recA locus at 100% efficiency using a double-stranded PCR product (Table 1). Such experiments were not performed on the tolC locus as additional manipulation was not required to demonstrate proof of principle.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 54 58 54 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 158 165 158 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 213 217 213 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 217 218 217 218 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 248 250 248 250 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 264 268 264 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 278 281 278 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ara</italic>
###xml 158 165 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
An alternative to colicin E1 for counter-selection of tolC was tried but did not yield favorable results. TLS phage uses TolC as a receptor for attachment to E. coli and following infection and replication inside tolC+ strains, TLS kills the cell (17). Removal of tolC from the ara locus was attempted using TLS phage counter-selection on agar plates and in broth. Individual recombinants often demonstrated weak phage resistance (upon purification and phage cross-streak) as well as the ability to retain resistance to SDS (data not shown). As the colicin E1 counter-selection provided favorable results and is not affected by unforeseen changes in surface lipopolysaccharides, further optimization of TLS phage for selection was not pursued.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 126 130 126 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">btuB</italic>
###xml 134 138 134 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 159 163 159 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">btuB</italic>
###xml 247 249 247 249 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 302 306 302 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">btuB</italic>
###xml 398 402 398 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 501 503 501 503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 635 639 635 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 723 727 723 727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 838 843 834 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58 B59 B60">58&#8211;60</xref>
###xml 1093 1097 1089 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1281 1287 1272 1278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 1289 1291 1280 1282 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 1379 1383 1370 1374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1398 1405 1389 1396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
Colicin E1 selection is not without drawbacks as E1-resistant (or tolerant) mutants can arise through spontaneous mutation of btuB or tolC. The involvement of btuB mutants can be identified easily by screening colonies in the plate receptor test (23) and patching on SDS-containing media. Mutations in btuB would appear colicin-resistant, but SDS-resistant as well. In addition, point mutations in tolC that interfere directly with colicin E1 binding and/or translocation but remain efflux competent (15) would also be identified through this counter-screen. In fact, most of the infrequent E1-resistant recombinants shown not to have tolC deletions by PCR fell into this category (data not shown). Particular mutations in tolC (L3S, DeltaL3, L412P, and C-terminal deletions) confer both novobiocin sensitivity and colicin E1 resistance (58-60), but none have been specifically reported for SDS and colicin E1. Nevertheless, such spontaneous mutations could interfere with efficient counter-selection using the method described in this work. Mutations at multiple loci (e.g. mutations in both tolC and an efflux pump) could also confound selection as such cells might be both colicin E1-resistant and SDS-sensitive. Given the extremely high recombination rates catalyzed by lambda redgam (28), these potential false positives were not problematic and efficient selection against tolC was possible (Table 1).
###end p 58
###begin p 59
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 226 230 226 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 322 326 322 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 549 557 549 557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 602 609 602 609 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 667 671 667 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 754 761 754 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 754 761 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Along the same lines, removal of the tolC cassette may occur through recombination at repetitive sequences flanking the intended deletion junctions. Such events occur irrespective of the counter-selectable marker used and the tolC strategy cannot overcome this inherent drawback of the system. Recombinants that have lost tolC expression through recombination at flanking repeats would also be colicin E1-resistant and would appear as false positives during selection. PCR testing with primers that bracket the proper deletion junction (as shown in Figure 2) would exclude these false positives. Thus, Table 1 reports efficiencies that reflect only proper removal of tolC from the targeted site. Interestingly, the highly homologous ribosomal operons of E. coli represent a situation where deletion through flanking repeats may occur (see subsequently).
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 29 33 29 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 203 210 203 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 361 364 361 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">not</italic>
###xml 675 679 671 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 753 757 749 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpsL</italic>
###xml 771 777 762 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 203 210 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
As mentioned previously, the tolC marker system does not require specialized media or small molecule antibiotics and can be used economically in laboratories familiar with the growth and manipulation of E. coli strains in the course of normal molecular biology protocols. A potential confounding factor of the technique is that antibiotic resistant markers are not needed. While this can be advantageous when studying physiological processes that may be altered by the presence of antibiotics, lack of antibiotics does permit the growth of contaminants in the absence of proper sterile technique. Should contamination be problematic, a straightforward conversion of the DeltatolC parent strain to streptomycin resistance by creating a point mutation in rpsL using lambda redgam may offer a solution.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 276 278 276 278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 543 555 543 555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli tolC</italic>
###xml 579 607 579 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Chromohalobacter marismortui</italic>
###xml 609 611 609 611 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 679 681 679 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 682 684 682 684 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 543 550 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 579 607 <span type="species:ncbi:42055">Chromohalobacter marismortui</span>
The strategy of colicin selection may have broader application to other model organisms where a dearth of genetic tools has hampered progress toward understanding molecular processes. For instance, some archaebacteria synthesize and respond to peptide toxins called halocins (19). The receptors and molecular targets of these toxins have not been fully characterized, but they may provide a similar set of tools for genome engineering in the archaea. In fact, an outer membrane protein with weak sequence homology but functional similarity to E. coli tolC has been identified in Chromohalobacter marismortui (61) Given that archaea are known to take up and recombine linear DNA (62,63), a gene disruption strategy similar to that described in this work may have potential.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 255 257 255 257 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 316 320 316 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">recA</italic>
###xml 339 343 339 343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 395 402 395 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 424 428 424 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dicB</italic>
###xml 501 503 501 503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B65">65</xref>
###xml 504 506 504 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B66">66</xref>
###xml 546 548 546 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B67">67</xref>
###xml 612 619 612 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 658 662 646 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">recA</italic>
###xml 665 667 653 655 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 805 807 793 795 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B69">69</xref>
###xml 808 810 796 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B70">70</xref>
###xml 813 820 801 808 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 856 860 844 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 892 896 880 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dicB</italic>
###xml 970 975 958 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dicB'</italic>
###xml 1104 1108 1092 1096 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ygeX</italic>
###xml 1193 1197 1181 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dicB</italic>
###xml 1199 1201 1187 1189 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 1240 1242 1228 1230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 1283 1287 1271 1275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">murA</italic>
###xml 1292 1296 1280 1284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metG</italic>
###xml 1349 1353 1337 1341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1452 1456 1440 1444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1588 1594 1576 1582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1596 1598 1584 1586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 612 619 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
As shown in the Results section, the tolC marker system can also be used to assess the essentiality and expression levels of various target genes through ORF-Xchange. A similar strategy was recently described in detail using antibiotic resistant markers (64). For a constitutively expressed, non-essential gene like recA, ORF-Xchange with tolC occurred at high frequency and was 100% efficient (Table 1). The product of the dicB gene stimulates MinC function and interferes with normal cell division (65,66). DicB synthesis is tightly regulated (67), and is one of the least abundant mRNAs/proteins found in the E. coli cell (approximately 60-fold less than recA) (68). Its essentiality has been questioned, however, as some groups have reported conflicting results using various experimental techniques (69,70). Table 1 shows that the promoter-containing tolC cassette is able to delete the dicB gene with 100% efficiency, confirming its non-essentiality. In addition, dicB's low expression level was confirmed by unsuccessful ORF-Xchange under standard SDS selection. Similar results were obtained for ygeX, a gene of unknown function whose expression levels are just slightly below that of dicB (68). In agreement with previous results (39), deletion of the known essential genes murA and metG could not be achieved with high frequency by either tolC cassette unless a complementing copy of either gene was provided. These data demonstrate that the tolC marker system can be used successfully to screen for gene essentiality and expression in the same manner as described by Bubunenko et al. (64).
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 179 186 179 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 199 207 199 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 377 378 377 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 379 381 379 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B71">71</xref>
###xml 538 547 538 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 557 559 557 559 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B72">72</xref>
###xml 684 686 684 686 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B73">73</xref>
###xml 894 896 894 896 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 897 899 897 899 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B74">74</xref>
###xml 179 186 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Perhaps the best demonstration of the utility and reproducibility of tolC selection/counter-selection is the seamless modifications made in six of the seven 23S rRNA genes on the E. coli chromosome (Figure 3). These genes occupy various positions on the genomic map and reside in complex operons interspersed between other essential structural rRNA and tRNA genes (Figure S3) (1,71). The intergenic sequences of the rRNA operons contain RNAse cleavage sites necessary for the correct processing and maturation of the individual cistrons (Figures 2 and S3) (72). In addition, there is a high degree of sequence homology among the RNA coding sequences and among the intergenic regions (73). Such features make directed genetic modification of the individual rRNA genes on the chromosome a challenging task. Previously published work was relegated to creating large deletions in the rRNA operons (46,74).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 28 32 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 117 124 117 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 193 199 188 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 235 240 230 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC'</italic>
###xml 368 372 363 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrlC</italic>
###xml 385 393 380 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 395 402 390 397 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 422 426 417 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 528 532 519 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrlC</italic>
###xml 672 678 654 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 869 873 851 855 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trpT</italic>
###xml 929 933 911 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trpT</italic>
###xml 1043 1051 1025 1033 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 117 124 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 170 190 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">bacteriophage lambda</span>
As this work describes, the tolC marker system provides the tools necessary to precisely remodel the rRNA operons in E. coli. The keys to this advancement are the use of bacteriophage lambda's redgam recombination system combined with tolC's selection properties: namely the ability to use rich media without traditional antibiotic markers. Successful deletion of the rrlC gene alone (Figure 2, Table 1) demonstrates that tolC modification of the ribosomal operons can be achieved without conferring polar effects. RS1443 (DeltarrlC strain) has a growth phenotype indistinguishable from RS537 (DeltarrnG), with no observable defect in protein synthesis, as maximal lambda redgam induction occurs within 15 min as seen with the parent strain (data not shown). Since the viability of RS1443 depends upon proper expression and processing of the essential tryptophan tRNA (trpT) gene located downstream, these results establish that trpT expression is not disturbed by the genetic manipulations performed and that the experimental design shown in Figure 2 is sound.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 73 81 73 81 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">recA</italic>
###xml 244 248 244 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnC</italic>
###xml 448 450 448 450 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B74">74</xref>
###xml 451 453 451 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B75">75</xref>
###xml 633 640 633 640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
Using this strategy, deletion of six 23S rRNA genes was straightforward (Figure 3). Mutations in any rRNA operon were maintained by preventing homogenotization through the use of the recA deleted, RS526 strain background. The decision to leave rrnC as the only intact operon was based on its proximity to the origin of DNA replication, with the intention that gene dosage effects might provide a more favorable growth rate to a single-copy mutant (74,75). In fact, the ability to perform these genetic manipulations in rich media was crucial as the growth rate of cells with decreased 23S rRNA gene copies was significantly reduced (Table 2). Interestingly, mutants with two to five copies of 23S rRNA genes had very similar growth rates (2.2% SD between strains) but were collectively approximately34% slower than their isogenic parent.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 51 54 51 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrl</italic>
###xml 84 91 84 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 228 234 223 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 706 712 687 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 1026 1028 1007 1009 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 1029 1031 1010 1012 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B75">75</xref>
###xml 84 91 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In addition to the effect on growth rate, deleting rrl genes from the chromosome of E. coli has a pronounced effect on protein synthesis. This was observed indirectly through assessment of the time required for sufficient lambdaredgam induction to yield recombinants at non-essential loci. For example, where a 15 min induction at 42degreesC yielded thousands of recombinants in the WT strain, a minimum of 60 min was required for strains having only one or two copies of the 23S rRNA gene (data not shown). The Delta5 strain (RS554) required 2.5x more time for induction than the Delta3 strain (RS547) while the single-copy strain (RS676), despite its even slower growth rate, was comparable to RS554 for redgam induction (data not shown). Given the unique construction of these mutants, decreases in 23S rRNA gene copy number may not yield predictable changes in growth rate and ribosome efficiency. Although the increase in doubling time is similar to that seen with other rRNA deletion strains reported in the literature (46,75), a direct comparison is difficult as the strains constructed here are not deleted for entire rRNA operons nor are plasmids used to provide essential functions to the cell. Therefore, a more thorough investigation of the physiological properties of these new mutants is required.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 150 158 150 158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 489 493 485 489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrlC</italic>
###xml 876 878 866 868 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B76">76</xref>
###xml 945 947 935 937 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B77">77</xref>
###xml 959 963 949 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdsA</italic>
###xml 1004 1006 994 996 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B78">78</xref>
###xml 1013 1017 1003 1007 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdsA</italic>
###xml 1340 1342 1330 1332 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B78">78</xref>
As a first step towards understanding the molecular basis of the mutant phenotypes, the ribosome profiles from select mutant strains were determined (Figure 4). Reducing the number of 23S rRNA genes affected the ribosome profiles of the mutants constructed in this work. The Delta3 mutant (having four copies of 23S rRNA genes), shows an increase in free 30S and 50S ribosomal subunits compared to WT but a reduced amount of 70S ribosomes. The effect is more pronounced in the single-copy rrlC strain RS676 where 70S ribosomes and free 50S subunits levels are further reduced compared to WT, but an excess of 30S subunits is present. This imbalance in ribosome content could account for the observations concerning growth rate and protein synthesis discussed in the previous paragraph. A similar imbalance has been detected in ribosomes from normal cells grown at 16degreesC (76), from cells over-expressing incomplete rRNA genes from plasmids (77), and from cdsA mutants when grown at low temperatures (78). The cdsA mutants, however, lead to accumulation of a 40S particle not yet seen with the mutants described in this work. In the studies where a 3' segment of 23S rRNA was expressed from a plasmid, it was determined that the material sedimenting at 30S was misfolded 23S rRNA bound to an incomplete complement of ribosomal proteins (78).
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 174 181 174 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 523 530 523 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 174 181 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The unbalanced ribosome profile of RS676 prompted a test of whether this strain (or any of the other mutants) showed altered sensitivity towards antibiotics that bind to the E. coli ribosome given the potential for excess free 30S ribosomal subunits to act as a sink for inhibitor binding. Coupled with reduced 50S and 70S ribosomes levels, this could make RS676 relatively resistant to antibiotics that target the 30S ribosomal subunit. Upon testing all mutant strains against a number of different drugs and antibiotics (Table 2), no clear difference was detected under the conditions used. Interestingly, antibiotics that target normal cellular processes not related to protein synthesis (e.g. DNA replication, transcription, cell wall biosynthesis) also showed no change in potency compared to wild-type. These data suggest that the rRNA mutants constructed do not suffer gross abnormalities in essential cellular pathways.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 126 128 126 128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B79">79</xref>
###xml 129 131 129 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B80">80</xref>
###xml 428 430 428 430 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B81">81</xref>
###xml 592 594 587 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B82">82</xref>
###xml 741 748 736 743 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 787 789 782 784 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B83">83</xref>
###xml 557 569 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">phage lambda</span>
###xml 741 748 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The control of ribosome synthesis occurs at many levels and it has been the focus of many comprehensive studies [reviewed in (79,80)]. Ribosomal RNA synthesis is regulated at both the initiation and termination steps of transcription. The P1P2 promoters (shared by all rRNA operons) are subject to the action of a transcriptional activator (Fis), the alarmone ppGpp and the concentration of initiating nucleotide triphosphates (81). To prevent premature termination of the untranslated rRNA transcripts, antitermination mechanisms (similar to those used by phage lambda), are also important (82). These and other potential control mechanisms work together to ensure that rRNA synthesis is proportional to the steady-state growth rate of the E. coli cell (growth-rate-dependent control) (83).
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 129 131 129 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B84">84</xref>
###xml 429 431 429 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B84">84</xref>
###xml 621 628 621 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 721 729 721 729 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 990 994 990 994 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 1082 1089 1082 1089 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 621 628 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1082 1089 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The synthesis of ribosomal proteins is regulated by negative feedback inhibition of translation by free, unassembled r-proteins (84). Ribosomal protein operons are multi-cistronic and contain the genes encoding both small and large r-proteins. In most cases, one r-protein within an operon functions as an autogenous translational repressor, binding to a site on the message and blocking synthesis of all proteins in the operon (84). Coupled with the growth-rate-dependent control of rRNA production, these mechanisms help balance the synthesis of r-proteins with rRNA and ensure the cooperative assembly of ribosomes in E. coli. Given the imbalance of ribosomal subunits noted for the single copy 23S rRNA mutant RS676 (Figure 4), it is tempting to speculate that remodeling of the rRNA operons in the manner described here has lead to a short-circuiting of the regulatory pathways that control ribosome synthesis. Further investigation of this and other rRNA mutants constructed with the tolC marker system will guide additional studies on the regulation of ribosome synthesis in E. coli.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 157 164 157 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 271 275 271 275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tolC</italic>
###xml 300 306 295 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">redgam</italic>
###xml 157 164 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Finally, the TolC selection method reported in this work can be broadly applied to genetic manipulation of any DNA substrate capable of amplification within E. coli. The construction of new plasmid vectors, point mutations, deletions and insertions is possible using the tolC marker system and lambdaredgam. The type and specific nature of the modifications are not limited by TolC selection. The method is highly reproducible and may serve as sufficient replacement for other current selection systems.
###end p 71
